{{row hover highlight}}
Opinion polling for the [[2024 United Kingdom general election]]<!-- DO NOT BOLD, see [[WP:SBE]] for further guidance --> was carried out by various organisations to gauge voting intention. Most of the polling companies listed are members of the [[British Polling Council]] (BPC) and abide by its disclosure rules. The opinion polls listed range from the [[2019 United Kingdom general election|previous election]] on 12 December 2019 to the election on Thursday, 4 July 2024.<ref name="politics-date-confirmed">{{cite web |date=22 May 2024 |title=Rishi Sunak announces 4 July general election |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/live/uk-politics-69042935 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240608214915/https://www.bbc.com/news/live/uk-politics-69042935 |archive-date=8 June 2024 |access-date=22 May 2024 |website=BBC News}}</ref>

== Graphical summaries ==
The Conservatives led the polls for the two years following the 2019 general election, which included [[Brexit withdrawal agreement|Brexit]], the onset of the [[COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom|COVID-19 pandemic]] and [[COVID-19 vaccination in the United Kingdom|vaccine rollout]] during the leadership of Boris Johnson. Labour took a lead following the [[Partygate]] scandal and maintained this through the [[Liz Truss]] and [[Rishi Sunak]] premierships until the 2024 election.
<div>{{Switcher|[[File:Opinion_polling_for_the_next_United_Kingdom_general_election_after_2019_(LOESS).svg|975px]]
|Opinion polls conducted for the 2024 United Kingdom general election from the 2019 general election with a local regressions (LOESS) trend line for each party.

==Guide to tables==
Poll results are listed in the tables below in reverse chronological order. The highest percentage figure in each poll is displayed in bold, and its background is shaded in the leading party's colour. The "lead" column shows the [[percentage point]] difference between the two parties with the highest figures. When a poll result is a tie, the figures with the highest percentages are shaded and displayed in bold.

"Green" in these tables refers to combined totals for the [[green parties in the United Kingdom]], namely the [[Green Party of England and Wales]], the [[Scottish Greens]], and, for polls of the entire UK, the [[Green Party Northern Ireland]]. The three parties share a commitment to environmental policies, but are independent of one another, with each contesting elections only in its own region.

The polling company ComRes was acquired by [[Savanta]] in July 2019.<ref>Jane Bainbridge, [https://www.research-live.com/article/news/comres-sold-to-savanta/id/5057132 "ComRes Sold To Savanta"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240609210004/https://www.research-live.com/article/news/comres-sold-to-savanta/id/5057132 |date=9 June 2024 }}, ''Research Live'', 1 August 2019. Retrieved 13 January 2024.</ref> It was rebranded as Savanta ComRes in November 2019<ref>{{Cite web |title=ComRes rebrands to Savanta ComRes {{!}} News |url=http://www.research-live.com/article/news/comres-rebrands-to-savanta-comres/id/5061492 |access-date=2024-07-05 |website=Research Live |language=en |archive-date=17 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240617125425/https://www.research-live.com/article/news/comres-rebrands-to-savanta-comres/id/5061492 |url-status=live}}</ref> and as Savanta in December 2022.<ref>Katie McQuater, [https://www.research-live.com/article/news/savanta-drops-comres-msi-youthsight-and-mindspark-brand-names/id/5106032 "Savanta Drops ComRes, MSI, Youthsight and Mindspark Brand Names"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240608220125/https://www.research-live.com/article/news/savanta-drops-comres-msi-youthsight-and-mindspark-brand-names/id/5106032 |date=8 June 2024 }}, ''Research Live'', 1 December 2022. Retrieved 13 January 2024.</ref> In August 2023, the [[market research]] company Omnisis rebranded its public polling arm as We Think.<ref>Mike Underwood, [https://www.omnisis.co.uk/polls/visit-wethink-the-new-home-for-polling-by-the-team-at-omnisis/ "Visit WeThink — the new home for polling by the team at Omnisis"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523005518/https://www.omnisis.co.uk/polls/visit-wethink-the-new-home-for-polling-by-the-team-at-omnisis/ |date=23 May 2024 }}, Omnisis, 30 August 2023. Retrieved 13 January 2024.</ref> In October 2023, the Norstat group acquired Panelbase.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Panelbase Message |url=https://www.panelbase.net/norstatfaqs |access-date=2024-02-01 |website=www.panelbase.net |archive-date=1 February 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240201095106/https://www.panelbase.net/norstatfaqs |url-status=live}}</ref> In November 2023, Kantar Public rebranded to [[Verian]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=Kantar Public rebrands globally to become Verian |url=https://www.veriangroup.com/press-release/kantar-public-rebrands-globally-to-become-verian |access-date=2024-06-20 |website=www.veriangroup.com |language=en |archive-date=28 February 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240228054651/https://www.veriangroup.com/press-release/kantar-public-rebrands-globally-to-become-verian |url-status=live}}</ref> None of these organisational changes entailed changes in methodology.

== National poll results ==
Most national opinion polls do not cover [[Northern Ireland]], which has [[List of political parties in Northern Ireland|different major political parties]] from the rest of the United Kingdom. This distinction is made in the tables below in the area column, where "GB" means [[Great Britain]] (England, Scotland and Wales), and "UK" means the entire [[United Kingdom]]. [[Plaid Cymru]] only stand candidates in [[Wales]] and the [[Scottish National Party]] (SNP) only stand candidates in [[Scotland]].

=== 2024 ===
When compared to the result, the final week of polls on average underestimated the Conservative and Lib Dem vote shares and overestimated the Labour and Reform vote shares. The projected SNP and Green vote shares were largely accurate.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Vincent |first1=Jonathan |title=Why did the pollsters overestimate Labour's vote? |url=https://www.ft.com/content/ed2513a0-435d-4e44-a912-9fd15b94ab7a |access-date=9 July 2024 |agency=Financial Times |date=9 July 2024 |archive-date=9 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240709125147/https://www.ft.com/content/ed2513a0-435d-4e44-a912-9fd15b94ab7a |url-status=live}}</ref>

=== Young voters ===
Savanta published polls of voters aged between 18 and 25. The 2019 result comes from the British Election Study's estimate of voters aged 18 to 24 and the 2024 result comes from Ipsos' estimate of voters among the same age group.

==== 16–17 year olds ====
JL Partners polled a sample of 16 and 17 year olds. The voting age in UK elections is 18, therefore none of the individuals polled had the legal right to vote. However, there was an active debate during the campaign on lowering the minimum voting age, and Labour included the policy in their manifesto.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Should 16- year-olds be allowed to vote in the general election? Join The Independent Debate |website=[[Independent.co.uk]] |date=4 June 2024 |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/voting-age-uk-16-keir-starmer-b2555856.html |access-date=2024-07-02 |url-status=live |archive-date=27 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240627135255/https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/voting-age-uk-16-keir-starmer-b2555856.html}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=The case for lowering the voting age to 16 |url=https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/politicsandpolicy/the-case-for-lowering-the-voting-age-to-16/ |access-date=2024-07-02 |url-status=live |archive-date=7 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240607120258/https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/politicsandpolicy/the-case-for-lowering-the-voting-age-to-16/}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=POLL: Should 16 year olds be allowed to vote in the UK? |date=28 May 2024 |url=https://www.bridgwatermercury.co.uk/news/24351204.poll-16-year-olds-allowed-vote-uk/ |access-date=2024-07-02 |url-status=live |archive-date=29 May 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240529055025/https://www.bridgwatermercury.co.uk/news/24351204.poll-16-year-olds-allowed-vote-uk/}}</ref><ref name="bbc.co.uk">{{Cite web |title=Lowering the voting age is important, youth says |date=14 June 2024 |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/articles/c9007edn144o |access-date=2024-07-02 |url-status=live |archive-date=17 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240617124520/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/articles/c9007edn144o}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=Shocking news: Daily Mail says public opposes Labour's votes-at-16 policy – here's why Starmer won't flinch |date=7 June 2024 |url=https://www.qmul.ac.uk/media/news/2024/hss/shocking-news-daily-mail-says-public-opposes-labours-votes-at-16-policy--heres-why-starmer-wont-flinch.html |access-date=2024-07-02 |url-status=live |archive-date=9 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240609184553/https://www.qmul.ac.uk/media/news/2024/hss/shocking-news-daily-mail-says-public-opposes-labours-votes-at-16-policy--heres-why-starmer-wont-flinch.html}}</ref>

== Seat projections ==
The general election was contested under the [[first-past the post]] electoral system in [[Constituencies of the Parliament of the United Kingdom|650 constituencies]]. 326 seats were needed for a parliamentary majority.

Most polls were reported in terms of the overall popular vote share, and the pollsters did not typically project how these shares would equate to numbers of seats in the House of Commons.

===Projections from aggregators===
Various models existed which continually projected election outcomes for the seats in Britain based on the aggregate of polling data. Final predictions of some notable models are tabulated below.

===MRP and SRP polls===
[[Multilevel regression with poststratification]] (MRP) was used by [[YouGov]] to predict outcomes for the 2017 and 2019 elections.<ref name="Cohen">{{cite news |last1=Cohen |first1=Daniel |title='I've never known voters be so promiscuous': the pollsters working to predict the next UK election |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2019/sep/27/voters-so-promiscuous-the-pollsters-working-to-predict-next-election |access-date=31 October 2019 |work=The Guardian |date=27 September 2019 |archive-date=11 September 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240911131900/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2019/sep/27/voters-so-promiscuous-the-pollsters-working-to-predict-next-election |url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=YouGov UK General Election MRP Estimates – February 2019 |url=https://d25d2506sfb94s.cloudfront.net/cumulus_uploads/document/416n3133f2/YouGov%20Feb%202019%20voting%20intention%20MRP.pdf |publisher=YouGov |date=11 February 2019 |access-date=22 May 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190212090317/https://d25d2506sfb94s.cloudfront.net/cumulus_uploads/document/416n3133f2/YouGov%20Feb%202019%20voting%20intention%20MRP.pdf |archive-date=12 February 2019 |url-status=live}}</ref> Multiple polling companies conducted such polling and modelling for the 2024 election, these are tabulated below. Also included is a stacked regression with poststratification (SRP) poll produced by J.L. Partners, the first time such a method has been used for a UK election.<ref>{{cite web |title=First J.L. Partners SRP Model Shows Labour On Course For A Landslide |url=https://jlpartners.co.uk/first-jl-partners-srp-model-shows-labour-on-course-for-a-landslide?s=09/ |publisher=J.L. Partners |access-date=30 June 2024 |archive-date=30 June 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630165135/https://jlpartners.co.uk/first-jl-partners-srp-model-shows-labour-on-course-for-a-landslide?s=09/ |url-status=live}}</ref> All of these polls use sample sizes substantially larger than typical national polls.

These polls were of Britain only, though the reporting of some results include the 18 Northern Irish seats under "Others". Polling companies also differ in their handling of the [[Speaker of the House of Commons (United Kingdom)#Seat in Parliament|Speaker's seat]], considering it variously as Labour, "Other", or omitting it from the results. Negative values in the rightmost "majority" column below indicate that the party with the most seats would have a [[Plurality (voting)|plurality]] of seats, but would [[minority government|not have a majority]]. The overall vote share values for these polls, where reported, are also included in the tables above.

==Exit poll==
An [[exit poll]] conducted by [[Ipsos]] for the [[BBC]], [[ITN|ITV]], and [[Sky News]] was published at the end of voting at 22:00, predicting the number of seats for each party.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Wheeler |first=Brian |date=4 July 2024 |title=Starmer set to be PM as Tories face worst defeat - exit poll |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cd1xnzlzz99o |access-date=4 July 2024 |website=BBC News |language=en-GB |archive-date=4 July 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240704210119/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cd1xnzlzz99o |url-status=live}}</ref>

The extent of Labour's victory was projected to be slightly less than seen in the last week of opinion polls, though still a substantial landslide. The exit poll ended up being close to the actual results, apart from the Reform figure which was slightly overestimated.
===BBC updated forecasts===
Throughout the night and into the early hours of 5 July, BBC News updated their forecast, combining the exit poll with the results coming in.<ref>{{Cite AV media |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4X13jmmsqBI |title=BBC UK General Election 2024 {{!}} Part 1 {{!}} 9:55pm to 2am {{!}} 4th July 2024 |date=2024-07-05 |last=Political TV |access-date=2024-08-26 |via=YouTube |archive-date=26 August 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240826023815/https://www.youtube.com/watch?app=desktop&v=4X13jmmsqBI |url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite AV media |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JktYCuYybLI |title=BBC UK General Election 2024 {{!}} Part 2 {{!}} 2am to 6am {{!}} 5th July 2024 |date=2024-07-05 |last=Political TV |access-date=2024-08-26 |via=YouTube |archive-date=26 August 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240826023815/https://www.youtube.com/watch?app=desktop&v=JktYCuYybLI |url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{Cite AV media |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=u8c_zCN8Xnk |title=BBC UK General Election 2024 {{!}} Part 3 {{!}} 6am to 8am {{!}} 5th July 2024 |date=2024-07-05 |last=Political TV |access-date=2024-08-26 |via=YouTube |archive-date=26 August 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240826023816/https://www.youtube.com/watch?app=desktop&v=u8c_zCN8Xnk |url-status=live}}</ref>
